Section 1:
UNOFFICIAL COPY 26 RS SB 122/EN
2 WHEREAS, it is the intent of this Commonwealth to promote, strengthen, and
3 encourage family life for the protection and care of children and to maintain the family
4 unit with an emphasis on the parent-child relationship; and
5 WHEREAS, the Commonwealth recognizes that parental incarceration is classified
6 as an adverse childhood experience. Multiple peer-reviewed studies demonstrate that
7 adverse childhood experiences contribute to poor mental and physical health outcomes
8 for children and increase the likelihood that a child will become involved with the
9 criminal justice system; and
10 WHEREAS, to prevent unnecessary harm to children caused by the separation from
11 a parent during incarceration, alternative sentences should be considered before a parent
12 is sentenced to a term of imprisonment; and
13 WHEREAS, this Act shall be interpreted to promote the family unit with an
14 emphasis on maintaining the parent-child relationship by providing mental health
15 treatment, substance use disorder treatment, parenting classes, educational or vocational
16 training, or other services, as appropriate, while ensuring public safety, reducing
17 recidivism, and making any victim whole through restitution;
18 NOW, THEREFORE,
19 Be it enacted by the General Assembly of the Commonwealth of Kentucky:
20 Section 1. KRS 533.010 is amended to read as follows:
21 (1) Any person who has been convicted of a crime and who has not been sentenced to
22 death may be sentenced to probation, probation with an alternative sentencing plan,
23 or conditional discharge as provided in this chapter.
24 (2) Before imposition of a sentence of imprisonment, the court shall consider
25 probation, probation with an alternative sentencing plan, or conditional discharge.
26 Unless the defendant is a violent felon as defined in KRS 439.3401 or a statute
27 prohibits probation, shock probation, or conditional discharge, after due
Page 1 of 87
SB012220.100 - 1929 - XXXX 3/31/2026 4:08 PM Engrossed
UNOFFICIAL COPY 26 RS SB 122/EN
1 consideration of the defendant's risk and needs assessment, nature and
2 circumstances of the crime, and the history, character, and condition of the
3 defendant, including whether the defendant is a caretaker, probation or
4 conditional discharge shall be granted, unless the court is of the opinion that
5 imprisonment is necessary for protection of the public because:
6 (a) There is substantial risk that during a period of probation or conditional
7 discharge the defendant will commit another crime;
8 (b) The defendant is in need of correctional treatment that can be provided most
9 effectively by [his ]commitment to a correctional institution; or
10 (c) A disposition under this chapter will unduly depreciate the seriousness of the
11 defendant's crime.
12 (3) In the event the court determines that probation is not appropriate after due
13 consideration of the defendant's risk and needs assessment, nature and
14 circumstances of the crime, and the history, character, and condition of the
15 defendant, including whether the defendant is a caretaker, probation with an
16 alternative sentencing plan shall be granted unless the court is of the opinion that
17 imprisonment is necessary for the protection of the public because:
18 (a) There is a likelihood that during a period of probation with an alternative
19 sentencing plan or conditional discharge the defendant will commit a Class D
20 or Class C felony or a substantial risk that the defendant will commit a Class
21 B or Class A felony;
22 (b) The defendant is in need of correctional treatment that can be provided most
23 effectively by commitment to a correctional institution; or
24 (c) A disposition under this chapter will unduly depreciate the seriousness of the
25 defendant's crime.
26 (4) The court shall not determine that there is a likelihood that the defendant will
27 commit a Class C or Class D felony based upon the defendant's risk and needs
Page 2 of 87
SB012220.100 - 1929 - XXXX 3/31/2026 4:08 PM Engrossed
UNOFFICIAL COPY 26 RS SB 122/EN
1 assessment and the fact that:
2 (a) The defendant has never been convicted of, pled guilty to, or entered an
3 Alford plea to a felony offense;
4 (b) If convicted of, having pled guilty to, or having entered an Alford plea to a
5 felony offense, the defendant successfully completed probation more than ten
6 (10) years immediately prior to the date of the commission of the felony for
7 which the defendant is now being sentenced and has had no intervening
8 convictions, pleas of guilty, or Alford pleas to any criminal offense during
9 that period; or
10 (c) The defendant has been released from incarceration for the commission of a
11 felony offense more than ten (10) years immediately prior to the date of the
12 commission of the felony for which the defendant is now being sentenced and
13 has had no intervening convictions, pleas of guilty, or Alford pleas to any
14 criminal offense during that period.
15 (5) In making a determination under subsection (4) of this section, the court may
16 determine that the greater weight of the evidence indicates that there is a likelihood
17 that the defendant will commit a Class C or Class D felony.
18 (6) In determining whether a defendant is a caretaker as described in subsections (2)
19 and (3) of this section, the court shall consider evidence presented to the court
20 that the defendant:
21 (a) Has consistently assumed responsibility for the housing, health, education,
22 safety, or support of a dependent child, family member, or any other person
23 identified by the court as being reliant on the defendant for support; or
24 (b) Is a woman who has given birth to a child while awaiting her sentencing
25 hearing, or who remains pregnant while awaiting her sentencing hearing.
26 (7) Upon initial sentencing of a defendant or upon modification or revocation of
27 probation, when the court deems it in the best interest of the public and the

1 defendant, the court may order probation with the defendant to serve one (1) of the
2 following alternative sentences:
3 (a) To a halfway house for no more than twelve (12) months;
4 (b) To home incarceration with or without work release for no more than twelve
5 (12) months;
6 (c) To jail for a period not to exceed twelve (12) months with or without work
7 release, community service and other programs as required by the court;
8 (d) To a residential treatment program for the abuse of alcohol or controlled
9 substances;
10 (e) To a reentry center for no more than twelve (12) months; or
11 (f) To any other specified counseling program, rehabilitation or treatment
12 program, or facility, including but not limited to one (1) of more of the
13 following:
14 1. Substance use disorder treatment and prevention services;
15 2. Domestic violence education and prevention services;
16 3. Child abuse treatment and prevention services;
17 4. Parenting classes;
18 5. Anger management;
19 6. Vocational and educational training;
20 7. Targeted case management services that assist with access to
21 transportation and affordable and safe housing;
22 8. Literacy and financial literacy training;
23 9. Individual counseling and therapy;
24 10. Family counseling when there is no known history of family or
25 intimate partner violence;
26 11. Referral to local domestic violence resources for voluntary
27 participation; and

1 12. Restorative practices designed to make the participant accountable to
2 the victim, when there is an identified victim and when it is safe to do
3 so.
4 (8)[(7)] If during the term of the alternative sentence the defendant fails to adhere to
5 and complete the conditions of the alternative sentence, the court may modify the
6 terms of the alternative sentence or may modify or revoke probation and alternative
7 sentence and commit the defendant to an institution.
8 (9)[(8)] In addition to those conditions that the court may impose, the conditions of
9 alternative sentence shall include the following and, if the court determines that the
10 defendant cannot comply with them, then they shall not be made available:
11 (a) A defendant sentenced to a halfway house shall:
12 1. Be working or pursuing his or her education or be enrolled in a full-time
13 treatment program;
14 2. Pay restitution during the term of probation; and
15 3. Have no contact with the victim of the defendant's crime;
16 (b) A defendant sentenced to home incarceration shall:
17 1. Be employed by another person or self-employed at the time of
18 sentencing to home incarceration and continue the employment
19 throughout the period of home incarceration, unless the court determines
20 that there is a compelling reason to allow home incarceration while the
21 defendant is unemployed;
22 2. Pay restitution during the term of home incarceration;
23 3. Enter a treatment program, if appropriate;
24 4. Pay all or some portion of the cost of home incarceration as determined
25 by the court;
26 5. Comply with other conditions as specified; and
27 6. Have no contact with the victim of the defendant's crime;
Page 5 of 87
SB012220.100 - 1929 - XXXX 3/31/2026 4:08 PM Engrossed
UNOFFICIAL COPY 26 RS SB 122/EN
1 (c) A defendant sentenced to jail with community service shall:
2 1. Pay restitution during all or some part of the defendant's term of
3 probation; and
4 2. Have no contact with the victim of the defendant's crime;
5 (d) A defendant sentenced to a residential treatment program for drug and alcohol
6 abuse shall:
7 1. Undergo mandatory drug screening during term of probation;
8 2. Be subject to active, supervised probation for a term of five (5) years;
9 3. Undergo aftercare as required by the treatment program;
10 4. Pay restitution during the term of probation; and
11 5. Have no contact with the victim of the defendant's crime; or
12 (e) A defendant sentenced to a reentry center shall:
13 1. Be employed in the community or working in a vocational program at
14 the reentry center;
15 2. Be enrolled in a treatment program;
16 3. Pay restitution, fees, and fines during the term of probation; and
17 4. Comply with other conditions as specified.
18 (10)[(9)] When the court deems it in the best interest of the defendant and the public,
19 the court may order the defendant[person] to work at community service related
20 projects under the terms and conditions specified in KRS 533.070. Work at
21 community service related projects shall be considered as a form of conditional
22 discharge.
23 (11)[(10)] Probation with alternative sentence shall not be available as set out in KRS
24 532.045 and 533.060, except as provided in KRS 533.030(6).
25 (12)[(11)] The court may utilize a community corrections program authorized or funded
26 under KRS Chapter 196 to provide services to any person released under this
27 section.

1 (13)[(12)] When the court deems it in the best interest of the defendant and the public,
2 the court may order the defendant to placement for probation monitoring by a
3 private agency. The private agency shall report to the court on the defendant's
4 compliance with his or her terms of probation or conditional discharge. The
5 defendant shall be responsible for any reasonable charges which the private agency
6 charges.
7 (14)[(13)] The jailer in each county incarcerating Class C or D felons may deny work
8 release privileges to any defendant for violating standards of discipline or other jail
9 regulations. The jailer shall report the action taken and the details of the violation
10 on which the action was based to the court of jurisdiction within five (5) days of the
11 violation.
12 (15)[(14)] The Department of Corrections shall, by administrative regulation, develop
13 written criteria for work release privileges granted under this section.
14 (16)[(15)] Reimbursement of incarceration costs shall be paid directly to the jailer in the
15 amount specified by written order of the court. Incarceration costs owed to the
16 Department of Corrections shall be paid through the circuit clerk.
17 (17)[(16)] The court shall enter into the record written findings of fact and conclusions
18 of law when considering implementation of any sentence under this section.
19 SECTION 2. A NEW SECTION OF KRS CHAPTER 403 IS CREATED TO
20 READ AS FOLLOWS:
21 In any proceeding for child custody under this chapter where the court has made a
22 finding that a party has committed domestic violence and abuse as defined in KRS
23 403.720 against another party to the proceeding or a child of the parties:
24 (1) The court shall not remove custody from or reduce the parenting time of the
25 nonoffending party to whom the child is bonded or attached if the court finds that
26 the:
27 (a) Nonoffending party is competent and not abusive; and
Page 7 of 87
SB012220.100 - 1929 - XXXX 3/31/2026 4:08 PM Engrossed
UNOFFICIAL COPY 26 RS SB 122/EN
1 (b) Removal would be solely for purposes of improving the relationship between
2 the child and the offending party; and
3 (2) Any order to remediate resistance of a child to contact with a violent or abusive
4 parent shall primarily address the behavior of that parent.
5 Section 3. KRS 403.270 is amended to read as follows:
6 (1) (a) As used in this chapter and KRS 405.020, unless the context requires
7 otherwise, "de facto custodian" means a person who has been shown by clear
8 and convincing evidence to have been the primary caregiver for, and financial
9 supporter of, a child who within the last two (2) years has resided with the
10 person for an aggregate period of six (6) months or more if the child is under
11 three (3) years of age and for an aggregate period of one (1) year or more if
12 the child is three (3) years of age or older or has been placed by the
13 Department for Community Based Services. Any period of time after a legal
14 proceeding has been commenced by a parent seeking to regain custody of the
15 child shall not be included in determining whether the child has resided with
16 the person for the required minimum period.
17 (b) A person shall not be a de facto custodian until a court determines by clear
18 and convincing evidence that the person meets the definition of de facto
19 custodian established in paragraph (a) of this subsection. Once a court
20 determines that a person meets the definition of de facto custodian, the court
21 shall give the person the same standing in custody matters that is given to
22 each parent under this section and KRS 403.280, 403.340, 403.350, 403.822,
23 and 405.020.
24 (2) The court shall determine custody in accordance with the best interests of the child
25 and equal consideration shall be given to each parent and to any de facto custodian.
26 Subject to KRS 403.315, there shall be a presumption, rebuttable by a
27 preponderance of evidence, that joint custody and equally shared parenting time is
Page 8 of 87
SB012220.100 - 1929 - XXXX 3/31/2026 4:08 PM Engrossed
UNOFFICIAL COPY 26 RS SB 122/EN
1 in the best interests[interest] of the child. If a deviation from equal parenting time is
2 warranted, the court shall construct a parenting time schedule which maximizes the
3 time each parent or de facto custodian has with the child and is consistent with
4 ensuring the child's welfare. [The court shall consider all relevant factors
5 including:]
6 (3) In making a determination of custody, the court shall, prior to consideration of
7 any other factors enumerated in subsection (4) of this section:
8 (a) Consider any allegations of:
9 1. Domestic violence and abuse as defined in KRS 403.720; or
10 2. An abused or neglected child as defined in KRS 600.020;
11 committed by one (1) party against another party or a child of the parties;
12 and
13 (b) Make written findings on the record as to the impact, if any, of the
14 allegations described in paragraph (a) of this subsection on the child.
15 (4) After making the consideration required in subsection (3) of this section, the
16 court shall consider all other factors relevant to the determination of custody
17 including:
18 (a) The wishes of the child's parent or parents, and any de facto custodian, as to
19 his or her custody;
20 (b) The wishes of the child as to his or her custodian, with due consideration
21 given to the influence a parent or de facto custodian may have over the child's
22 wishes;
23 (c) The interaction and interrelationship of the child with his or her parent or
24 parents, his or her siblings, and any other person who may significantly affect
25 the child's best interests;
26 (d) The motivation of the adults participating in the custody proceeding;
27 (e) The child's adjustment and continuing proximity to his or her home, school,
Page 9 of 87
SB012220.100 - 1929 - XXXX 3/31/2026 4:08 PM Engrossed
UNOFFICIAL COPY 26 RS SB 122/EN
1 and community;
2 (f) The mental and physical health of all individuals involved;
3 (g) A finding by the court that domestic violence and abuse, as defined in KRS
4 403.720, has been committed by one (1) of the parties against a child of the
5 parties or against another party. The court shall determine the extent to which
6 the domestic violence and abuse has affected the child and the child's
7 relationship to each party, with due consideration given to efforts made by a
8 party toward the completion of any domestic violence treatment, counseling,
9 or program;
10 (h) A finding by the court that a party has maliciously made an intentionally
11 false allegation of child abuse which has no basis in fact and which the
12 party knew had no basis in fact against another party;
13 (i)[(h)] The extent to which the child has been cared for, nurtured, and
14 supported by any de facto custodian;
15 (j)[(i)] The intent of the parent or parents in placing the child with a de facto
16 custodian;
17 (k)[(j)] The circumstances under which the child was placed or allowed to
18 remain in the custody of a de facto custodian, including whether the parent
19 now seeking custody was previously prevented from doing so as a result of
20 domestic violence as defined in KRS 403.720 and whether the child was
21 placed with a de facto custodian to allow the parent now seeking custody to
22 seek employment, work, or attend school; and
23 (l)[(k)] The likelihood a party will allow the child frequent, meaningful, and
24 continuing contact with the other parent or de facto custodian, except that the
25 court shall not consider this likelihood if there is a finding that the other
26 parent or de facto custodian engaged in domestic violence and abuse, as
27 defined in KRS 403.720, against the party or a child and that a continuing
Page 10 of 87
SB012220.100 - 1929 - XXXX 3/31/2026 4:08 PM Engrossed
UNOFFICIAL COPY 26 RS SB 122/EN
1 relationship with the other parent will endanger the health or safety of either
2 that party or the child.
3 (5)[(3)] The abandonment of the family residence by a custodial party shall not be
4 considered where that[said] party was physically harmed or was seriously
5 threatened with physical harm by his or her spouse, when the[such] harm or threat
6 of harm was causally related to the abandonment.
7 (6)[(4)] If the court grants custody to a de facto custodian, the de facto custodian shall
8 have legal custody under the laws of the Commonwealth.
9 Section 4. KRS 403.290 is amended to read as follows:
10 (1) The court may interview the child in chambers to ascertain the child's wishes as to
11 his or her custodian and as to visitation. The court may permit counsel to be present
12 at the interview. The court shall cause a record of the interview to be made and to
13 be part of the record in the case.
14 (2) The court may seek the advice of professional personnel, whether or not employed
15 by the court on a regular basis. The advice given shall be in writing and made
16 available by the court to counsel upon request. Counsel may examine as a witness
17 any professional personnel consulted by the court.
18 (3) (a) Paid visitation supervisors and parenting coordinators in a custody
19 proceeding under this chapter, whether appointed by the court or engaged
20 by one (1) or more parties, shall document participation training focused on
21 the following:
22 1. Early childhood, child, and adolescent development;
23 2. Dynamics of domestic violence;
24 3. Effects of domestic violence on adult and child victims;
25 4. Lethality and risk issues;
26 5. Model protocols for addressing domestic violence;
27 6. Available community resources and victim services; and
Page 11 of 87
SB012220.100 - 1929 - XXXX 3/31/2026 4:08 PM Engrossed
UNOFFICIAL COPY 26 RS SB 122/EN
1 7. For paid visitation supervisors, the role of the paid supervisor and
2 ethical principles of supervising visitation.
3 (b) The training described in paragraph (a) of this subsection shall consist of:
4 1. Sixteen (16) hours of initial training before the paid visitation
5 supervisor or parenting coordinator is eligible to provide services to a
6 party to a custody proceeding; and
7 2. Eight (8) hours annually thereafter.
8 Section 5. KRS 403.315 is amended to read as follows:
9 (1) When determining or modifying a custody order pursuant to KRS 403.270,
10 403.280, 403.340, or 403.740, the court shall consider the safety and well-being of
11 the parties and of the children. If a domestic violence order is being or has been
12 entered against a party by another party or on behalf of a child at issue in the
13 custody hearing, the presumption that joint custody and equally shared parenting
14 time is in the best interests[interest] of the child shall not apply as to the party
15 against whom the domestic violence order is being or has been entered. The court
16 shall weigh all factors set out in Section 3 of this Act[ KRS 403.270(2)] in
17 determining the best interests[interest] of the child.
18 (2) There shall be a presumption, rebuttable by a preponderance of the evidence, that
19 joint custody and equally shared parenting time is not in the best interests of the
20 child if the court finds that a party has committed two (2) or more acts of
21 domestic violence and abuse as defined in KRS 403.720 against another party.
22 (3) (a) The court shall not make an award of custody or grant unsupervised
23 visitation with the child to a party who is found to have committed two (2) or
24 more acts of domestic violence or abuse as defined in KRS 403.720 against
25 another party unless that party has:
26 1. Completed:
27 a. A batterer's intervention program provided by a certified
Page 12 of 87
SB012220.100 - 1929 - XXXX 3/31/2026 4:08 PM Engrossed
UNOFFICIAL COPY 26 RS SB 122/EN
1 provider pursuant to 920 KAR 5:020;
2 b. Parenting classes; and
3 c. Substance use and mental health assessments and any
4 recommended corresponding treatments; and
5 2. Participated in supervised visitation.
6 (b) Following a party's completion of the requirements in paragraph (a) of this
7 subsection, the court shall conduct an evidentiary hearing before ordering
8 unsupervised visitation to that party and a second or subsequent hearing
9 before awarding custodial rights to that party.
10 Section 6. KRS 403.727 is amended to read as follows:
11 (1) Any petition filed under KRS 403.725 on behalf of a minor who is alleged to be a
12 victim of domestic violence and abuse, or in which a minor is named as a
13 respondent or petitioner, shall comply with the requirements in that section and
14 shall:
15 (a) Proceed in accordance with the procedural safeguards under KRS 610.070;
16 and
17 (b) Conform to the confidentiality provisions under KRS 610.340.
18 (2) (a) If the court orders an evidentiary hearing under KRS 403.730(1)(a), a
19 guardian ad litem shall be appointed for any unrepresented minor who is a
20 respondent to the action or a petitioner who is an alleged victim of domestic
21 violence and abuse.
22 (b) The guardian ad litem shall be paid a fee fixed by the court not to exceed five
23 hundred dollars ($500), which shall be paid by the Finance and
24 Administration Cabinet.
25 (3) A victim advocate as defined in KRS 421.570:
26 (a) Shall be permitted to attend the evidentiary hearing to offer advocacy
27 services pursuant to KRS 421.575 to the minor petitioner or the adult who
Page 13 of 87

UNOFFICIAL COPY 26 RS SB 122/EN
1 has filed the petition on behalf of the minor; and
2 (b) Shall not be excluded from the evidentiary hearing unless the:
3 1. Minor petitioner or adult who has filed the petition on behalf of the
4 minor declines the services offered; or
5 2. Court, upon motion and for good cause shown, determines that the
6 exclusion is in the best interests of the minor petitioner.
7 (4)[(3)] Violation of the terms or conditions of an order of protection issued under
8 KRS 403.740 after the person has been served or given notice of the order shall
9 constitute contempt of court and may constitute a criminal offense pursuant to KRS
10 403.763 if the offender is an adult or a public offense under KRS 600.020[(51)] if
11 the offender is a juvenile. Once a juvenile action or contempt proceeding has been
12 initiated, the other shall not be undertaken regardless of the outcome of the original
13 proceeding.
14 (5)[(4)] Nothing in subsection (4)[(3)] of this section shall preclude the
15 Commonwealth from proceeding, or the petitioner from pursuing charges, against
16 the minor respondent for offenses other than a violation of an order of protection.
17 Proceedings against a minor respondent for offenses other than a violation of an
18 order of protection shall proceed:
19 (a) In the juvenile session of District Court; and
20 (b) In accordance with the procedural and statutory provisions established for the
21 juvenile session of District Court.

7 Section 8. KRS 202A.011 is amended to read as follows:
8 As used in this chapter, unless the context otherwise requires:
9 (1) "Authorized staff physician" means a physician who is a bona fide member of the
10 hospital's medical staff;
11 (2) "Benefit from treatment" means the desired outcomes of treatment in a
12 psychiatric hospital for an individual with a mental illness, including but not
13 limited to:
14 (a) Symptom management and increased stability;
15 (b) A lessening of irrational thoughts and behaviors;
16 (c) Reduced risk of harm; or
17 (d) Acquisition of skills for self-care and for interacting and living in the
18 community;
19 (3) "Cabinet" means the [Kentucky ]Cabinet for Health and Family Services;
20 (4)[(3)] "Contract mental health evaluator" means a qualified mental health
21 professional who is employed by or under contract with a community mental health
22 center, crisis stabilization unit, mental institution, or any other facility designated by
23 the secretary to provide mental health evaluations to determine whether an
24 individual meets the criteria for involuntary hospitalization;
25 (5)[(4)] "Danger" or "threat of danger to self, family, or others" means, as a result of
26 mental illness, a person:
27 (a) Presents a substantial risk of serious physical harm to[or threat of substantial
Page 16 of 87
SB012220.100 - 1929 - XXXX 3/31/2026 4:08 PM Engrossed
UNOFFICIAL COPY 26 RS SB 122/EN
1 physical harm upon] self, family, or others as evidenced by recent behavior,
2 threats, or conduct demonstrating such risk;[,]
3 (b) Has attempted or threatened suicide or has expressed suicidal ideations and
4 there is a reasonable probability of serious self-harm unless prompt and
5 adequate treatment is provided;
6 (c) Is unable without supervision or assistance to provide for[including actions
7 which deprive self, family, or others of the] basic personal needs,[means of
8 survival] including provision for reasonable shelter, food, [or ]clothing, or
9 medical care, so that there exists a substantial likelihood of death, serious
10 physical injury, or serious physical debilitation. For purposes of this
11 paragraph, a person shall be deemed unable to provide for basic personal
12 needs even if a guardian, family member, or friend is willing and able to
13 provide assistance; or
14 (d) Is experiencing psychiatric deterioration, demonstrated by a substantial
15 decline in functioning from the person's baseline, such that the person's
16 judgment, insight, or ability to recognize the need for treatment is impaired,
17 and without intervention, the person's condition will predictably result in:
18 1. A substantial risk of serious physical harm to self, family, or others;
19 2. Serious physical debilitation or self-neglect; or
20 3. Further loss of ability to engage in safe or necessary self-care or to

20 record. The court, upon motion of the county attorney or the court's own
21 motion, shall conduct a review hearing:
22 1. To determine if the discharge plan gives the respondent a realistic
23 opportunity to avoid imminent readmittance into an inpatient
24 psychiatric hospital for treatment; and
25 2. At the earliest practicable time, consistent with due process and the
26 availability of counsel, and in no event later than seven (7) days after
27 the motion is made, except with the respondent's consent or upon the

SB012220.100 - 1929 - XXXX 3/31/2026 4:08 PM Engrossed
UNOFFICIAL COPY 26 RS SB 122/EN
1 court's finding that extraordinary circumstances exist and that delay is
2 indispensable to protect the respondent and the community.
3 (b) This hearing shall only be conducted for a respondent who within the past
4 twelve (12) months has been found incompetent to stand trial in a criminal
5 proceeding and has not been committed under KRS Chapter 202C.
6 (2) The court shall verify that discharge planning procedures were completed to give
7 the respondent a realistic opportunity to avoid recurrence of substantial symptom
8 burden that would necessitate psychiatric hospitalization. Those procedures shall
9 include but not be limited to any of the following:
10 (a) Documenting the housing status of the respondent or that housing services
11 were offered and the respondent declined;
12 (b) Scheduling an outpatient treatment appointment for no later than seven (7)
13 days after discharge;
14 (c) Providing or prescribing a thirty (30) day supply of medication;
15 (d) Documenting a transportation plan that may include securing a bus pass,
16 taxi voucher, or an acknowledgment that the respondent will walk or the
17 respondent's family will provide transportation;
18 (e) Developing and documenting a crisis plan with contact information for
19 services that are available twenty-four (24) hours a day;
20 (f) Developing a transfer of care plan or attempting to develop a transfer of
21 care plan with the respondent if the respondent has met with an outpatient
22 provider or an appointment with the outpatient provider has been
23 scheduled; or
24 (g) Contacting the respondent's family or other support systems, if the
25 respondent consents.
26 (3) For respondents with decision-making capacity who refuse housing or other
27 services under subsection (2) of this section, the discharge plan shall document:

1 (a) That housing and other services were offered and explained;

3 (c) That the respondent understands the potential consequences of his or her
4 choices;

6 contacts, mobile crisis services, drop-in services, and other safety-oriented
7 resources; and

9 1. Petition is dismissed; and
10 2. Court has ordered a respondent to court-ordered outpatient or any
11 other reasonable conditions;
12 (c) The length of time a respondent receives treatment under this chapter prior
13 to discharge by a hospital or termination of an order to receive outpatient
14 treatment; and
15 (d) A summary of the services provided to a respondent who is ordered to
16 involuntary hospitalization or to receive outpatient treatment.
17 (2) Any hospital, qualified mental health professional, and any other mental health
18 agency who evaluates or treats a respondent under this chapter shall be required
19 to report data to the cabinet as required under this section. The cabinet shall
20 promulgate administrative regulations in accordance with KRS Chapter 13A to
21 implement this section.
22 (3) The cabinet and the Administrative Office of the Courts shall enter into an
23 agreement to share data necessary to prepare the report required under this
24 section.
25 (4) The report prepared under this section shall not identify specific individuals.

5 (f) The payment or the failure to pay a reasonable portion of substitute physical
6 care and maintenance if financially able to do so.
7 (4) If the child has been placed with the cabinet, the parent may present testimony
8 concerning the reunification, adaptive or supportive services offered by the cabinet,
9 and whether additional services would be likely to bring about lasting parental
10 adjustment enabling a return of the child to the parent.
11 (5) If the parent proves by a preponderance of the evidence that the child will not
12 continue to be an abused or neglected child as defined in KRS 600.020[(1)] if
13 returned to the parent, or if the parent proves by a preponderance of the evidence
14 that appropriate and specifically targeted adaptive or supportive services based
15 upon an individual assessment of the parent have not been offered or provided to
16 the parent, the court in its discretion may determine not to terminate parental rights.
17 (6) Upon the conclusion of proof and argument of counsel, the Circuit Court shall enter
18 findings of fact, conclusions of law, and a decision as to each parent-respondent
19 within thirty (30) days either:
20 (a) Terminating the right of the parent; or
21 (b) Dismissing the petition and stating whether the child shall be returned to the
22 parent or shall remain in the custody of the state.
23 Section 40. KRS 202A.006 is amended to read as follows:
24 This chapter may be cited as the ["]Kentucky Mental Health Treatment[Hospitalization]
25 Act.["]
26 Section 41. The following KRS section is repealed:
27 202A.081 Court-ordered community-based outpatient treatment.

1 Section 42. By November 1, 2026, the Cabinet for Health and Family Services
2 shall provide a report to the Legislative Research Commission for referral to the Interim
3 Joint Committee on Health Services and the Interim Joint Committee on Judiciary
4 describing the existing services, treatments, and supports for mental illness and serious
5 mental illness available to persons who are subject to proceedings under KRS Chapter
6 202A and 202C and making recommendations for ways to strengthen, increase, and
7 broaden these services, treatments, and supports as appropriate. The descriptions shall
8 include type of providers, eligibility criteria, accessibility, and geographical locations of
9 the services, treatments, and supports.
10 Section 43. The Cabinet for Health and Family Services and Department for
11 Behavioral Health, Developmental and Intellectual Disabilities shall engage the services
12 of the Treatment Advocacy Center to develop and implement a statewide training
13 program to facilitate implementation of Sections 8 to 41 of this Act and ensure consistent
14 application of Sections 8 to 41 of this Act across state and local agencies.
15 Section 44. Section 1 of this Act may be cited as the Family Preservation and
16 Accountability Act.
17 Section 45. Section 4 of this Act takes effect January 1, 2027.
18 Section 46. Sections 8 to 41 and 43 of this Act take effect October 1, 2026.

UNOFFICIAL COPY 26 RS SB 122/EN
1 AN ACT relating to judicial proceedings.
2 WHEREAS, it is the intent of this Commonwealth to promote, strengthen, and
3 encourage family life for the protection and care of children and to maintain the family
4 unit with an emphasis on the parent-child relationship; and
5 WHEREAS, the Commonwealth recognizes that parental incarceration is classified
6 as an adverse childhood experience. Multiple peer-reviewed studies demonstrate that
7 adverse childhood experiences contribute to poor mental and physical health outcomes
8 for children and increase the likelihood that a child will become involved with the
9 criminal justice system; and
10 WHEREAS, to prevent unnecessary harm to children caused by the separation from
11 a parent during incarceration, alternative sentences should be considered before a parent
12 is sentenced to a term of imprisonment; and
13 WHEREAS, this Act shall be interpreted to promote the family unit with an
14 emphasis on maintaining the parent-child relationship by providing mental health
15 treatment, substance use disorder treatment, parenting classes, educational or vocational
16 training, or other services, as appropriate, while ensuring public safety, reducing
17 recidivism, and making any victim whole through restitution;
18 NOW, THEREFORE,
19 Be it enacted by the General Assembly of the Commonwealth of Kentucky:
20 Section 1. KRS 533.010 is amended to read as follows:
21 (1) Any person who has been convicted of a crime and who has not been sentenced to
22 death may be sentenced to probation, probation with an alternative sentencing plan,
23 or conditional discharge as provided in this chapter.
24 (2) Before imposition of a sentence of imprisonment, the court shall consider
25 probation, probation with an alternative sentencing plan, or conditional discharge.
26 Unless the defendant is a violent felon as defined in KRS 439.3401 or a statute
27 prohibits probation, shock probation, or conditional discharge, after due
Page 1 of 87
SB012220.100 - 1929 - XXXX 3/31/2026 4:08 PM Engrossed

UNOFFICIAL COPY 26 RS SB 122/EN
1 consideration of the defendant's risk and needs assessment, nature and
2 circumstances of the crime, and the history, character, and condition of the
3 defendant, including whether the defendant is a caretaker, probation or
4 conditional discharge shall be granted, unless the court is of the opinion that
5 imprisonment is necessary for protection of the public because:
6 (a) There is substantial risk that during a period of probation or conditional
7 discharge the defendant will commit another crime;
8 (b) The defendant is in need of correctional treatment that can be provided most
9 effectively by [his ]commitment to a correctional institution; or
10 (c) A disposition under this chapter will unduly depreciate the seriousness of the
11 defendant's crime.
12 (3) In the event the court determines that probation is not appropriate after due
13 consideration of the defendant's risk and needs assessment, nature and
14 circumstances of the crime, and the history, character, and condition of the
15 defendant, including whether the defendant is a caretaker, probation with an
16 alternative sentencing plan shall be granted unless the court is of the opinion that
17 imprisonment is necessary for the protection of the public because:
18 (a) There is a likelihood that during a period of probation with an alternative
19 sentencing plan or conditional discharge the defendant will commit a Class D
20 or Class C felony or a substantial risk that the defendant will commit a Class
21 B or Class A felony;
22 (b) The defendant is in need of correctional treatment that can be provided most
23 effectively by commitment to a correctional institution; or
24 (c) A disposition under this chapter will unduly depreciate the seriousness of the
25 defendant's crime.
26 (4) The court shall not determine that there is a likelihood that the defendant will
27 commit a Class C or Class D felony based upon the defendant's risk and needs
Page 2 of 87
SB012220.100 - 1929 - XXXX 3/31/2026 4:08 PM Engrossed

UNOFFICIAL COPY 26 RS SB 122/EN
1 assessment and the fact that:
2 (a) The defendant has never been convicted of, pled guilty to, or entered an
3 Alford plea to a felony offense;
4 (b) If convicted of, having pled guilty to, or having entered an Alford plea to a
5 felony offense, the defendant successfully completed probation more than ten
6 (10) years immediately prior to the date of the commission of the felony for
7 which the defendant is now being sentenced and has had no intervening
8 convictions, pleas of guilty, or Alford pleas to any criminal offense during
9 that period; or
10 (c) The defendant has been released from incarceration for the commission of a
11 felony offense more than ten (10) years immediately prior to the date of the
12 commission of the felony for which the defendant is now being sentenced and
13 has had no intervening convictions, pleas of guilty, or Alford pleas to any
14 criminal offense during that period.
15 (5) In making a determination under subsection (4) of this section, the court may
16 determine that the greater weight of the evidence indicates that there is a likelihood
17 that the defendant will commit a Class C or Class D felony.
18 (6) In determining whether a defendant is a caretaker as described in subsections (2)
19 and (3) of this section, the court shall consider evidence presented to the court
20 that the defendant:
21 (a) Has consistently assumed responsibility for the housing, health, education,
22 safety, or support of a dependent child, family member, or any other person
23 identified by the court as being reliant on the defendant for support; or
24 (b) Is a woman who has given birth to a child while awaiting her sentencing
25 hearing, or who remains pregnant while awaiting her sentencing hearing.
26 (7) Upon initial sentencing of a defendant or upon modification or revocation of
27 probation, when the court deems it in the best interest of the public and the

1 defendant, the court may order probation with the defendant to serve one (1) of the
2 following alternative sentences:
3 (a) To a halfway house for no more than twelve (12) months;
4 (b) To home incarceration with or without work release for no more than twelve
5 (12) months;
6 (c) To jail for a period not to exceed twelve (12) months with or without work
7 release, community service and other programs as required by the court;
8 (d) To a residential treatment program for the abuse of alcohol or controlled
9 substances;
10 (e) To a reentry center for no more than twelve (12) months; or

18 5. Anger management;

20 7. Targeted case management services that assist with access to

22 8. Literacy and financial literacy training;
23 9. Individual counseling and therapy;
24 10. Family counseling when there is no known history of family or

4 (8)[(7)] If during the term of the alternative sentence the defendant fails to adhere to
5 and complete the conditions of the alternative sentence, the court may modify the
6 terms of the alternative sentence or may modify or revoke probation and alternative
7 sentence and commit the defendant to an institution.
8 (9)[(8)] In addition to those conditions that the court may impose, the conditions of
9 alternative sentence shall include the following and, if the court determines that the
10 defendant cannot comply with them, then they shall not be made available:
11 (a) A defendant sentenced to a halfway house shall:
12 1. Be working or pursuing his or her education or be enrolled in a full-time
13 treatment program;
14 2. Pay restitution during the term of probation; and
15 3. Have no contact with the victim of the defendant's crime;
16 (b) A defendant sentenced to home incarceration shall:
17 1. Be employed by another person or self-employed at the time of
18 sentencing to home incarceration and continue the employment
19 throughout the period of home incarceration, unless the court determines
20 that there is a compelling reason to allow home incarceration while the
21 defendant is unemployed;
22 2. Pay restitution during the term of home incarceration;
23 3. Enter a treatment program, if appropriate;
24 4. Pay all or some portion of the cost of home incarceration as determined
25 by the court;
26 5. Comply with other conditions as specified; and
27 6. Have no contact with the victim of the defendant's crime;

1 (c) A defendant sentenced to jail with community service shall:
2 1. Pay restitution during all or some part of the defendant's term of
3 probation; and
4 2. Have no contact with the victim of the defendant's crime;
5 (d) A defendant sentenced to a residential treatment program for drug and alcohol
6 abuse shall:
7 1. Undergo mandatory drug screening during term of probation;
8 2. Be subject to active, supervised probation for a term of five (5) years;
9 3. Undergo aftercare as required by the treatment program;
10 4. Pay restitution during the term of probation; and
11 5. Have no contact with the victim of the defendant's crime; or
12 (e) A defendant sentenced to a reentry center shall:
13 1. Be employed in the community or working in a vocational program at
14 the reentry center;
15 2. Be enrolled in a treatment program;
16 3. Pay restitution, fees, and fines during the term of probation; and
17 4. Comply with other conditions as specified.
18 (10)[(9)] When the court deems it in the best interest of the defendant and the public,
19 the court may order the defendant[person] to work at community service related
20 projects under the terms and conditions specified in KRS 533.070. Work at
21 community service related projects shall be considered as a form of conditional
22 discharge.
23 (11)[(10)] Probation with alternative sentence shall not be available as set out in KRS
24 532.045 and 533.060, except as provided in KRS 533.030(6).
25 (12)[(11)] The court may utilize a community corrections program authorized or funded
26 under KRS Chapter 196 to provide services to any person released under this

19 SECTION 2. A NEW SECTION OF KRS CHAPTER 403 IS CREATED TO
20 READ AS FOLLOWS:
21 In any proceeding for child custody under this chapter where the court has made a
22 finding that a party has committed domestic violence and abuse as defined in KRS
23 403.720 against another party to the proceeding or a child of the parties:
24 (1) The court shall not remove custody from or reduce the parenting time of the
25 nonoffending party to whom the child is bonded or attached if the court finds that
26 the:
27 (a) Nonoffending party is competent and not abusive; and
Page 7 of 87
SB012220.100 - 1929 - XXXX 3/31/2026 4:08 PM Engrossed

UNOFFICIAL COPY 26 RS SB 122/EN
1 (b) Removal would be solely for purposes of improving the relationship between
2 the child and the offending party; and
3 (2) Any order to remediate resistance of a child to contact with a violent or abusive
4 parent shall primarily address the behavior of that parent.
5 Section 3. KRS 403.270 is amended to read as follows:
6 (1) (a) As used in this chapter and KRS 405.020, unless the context requires
7 otherwise, "de facto custodian" means a person who has been shown by clear
8 and convincing evidence to have been the primary caregiver for, and financial
9 supporter of, a child who within the last two (2) years has resided with the
10 person for an aggregate period of six (6) months or more if the child is under
11 three (3) years of age and for an aggregate period of one (1) year or more if
12 the child is three (3) years of age or older or has been placed by the
13 Department for Community Based Services. Any period of time after a legal
14 proceeding has been commenced by a parent seeking to regain custody of the
15 child shall not be included in determining whether the child has resided with
16 the person for the required minimum period.
17 (b) A person shall not be a de facto custodian until a court determines by clear
18 and convincing evidence that the person meets the definition of de facto
19 custodian established in paragraph (a) of this subsection. Once a court
20 determines that a person meets the definition of de facto custodian, the court
21 shall give the person the same standing in custody matters that is given to
22 each parent under this section and KRS 403.280, 403.340, 403.350, 403.822,
23 and 405.020.
24 (2) The court shall determine custody in accordance with the best interests of the child
25 and equal consideration shall be given to each parent and to any de facto custodian.
26 Subject to KRS 403.315, there shall be a presumption, rebuttable by a
27 preponderance of evidence, that joint custody and equally shared parenting time is

1 in the best interests[interest] of the child. If a deviation from equal parenting time is
2 warranted, the court shall construct a parenting time schedule which maximizes the
3 time each parent or de facto custodian has with the child and is consistent with
4 ensuring the child's welfare. [The court shall consider all relevant factors
5 including:]
6 (3) In making a determination of custody, the court shall, prior to consideration of
7 any other factors enumerated in subsection (4) of this section:
8 (a) Consider any allegations of:
9 1. Domestic violence and abuse as defined in KRS 403.720; or
10 2. An abused or neglected child as defined in KRS 600.020;
11 committed by one (1) party against another party or a child of the parties;
12 and
13 (b) Make written findings on the record as to the impact, if any, of the
14 allegations described in paragraph (a) of this subsection on the child.
15 (4) After making the consideration required in subsection (3) of this section, the
16 court shall consider all other factors relevant to the determination of custody

18 (a) The wishes of the child's parent or parents, and any de facto custodian, as to

26 (d) The motivation of the adults participating in the custody proceeding;
27 (e) The child's adjustment and continuing proximity to his or her home, school,

1 and community;
2 (f) The mental and physical health of all individuals involved;
3 (g) A finding by the court that domestic violence and abuse, as defined in KRS
4 403.720, has been committed by one (1) of the parties against a child of the
5 parties or against another party. The court shall determine the extent to which

10 (h) A finding by the court that a party has maliciously made an intentionally

1 relationship with the other parent will endanger the health or safety of either

3 (5)[(3)] The abandonment of the family residence by a custodial party shall not be

7 (6)[(4)] If the court grants custody to a de facto custodian, the de facto custodian shall

9 Section 4. KRS 403.290 is amended to read as follows:
10 (1) The court may interview the child in chambers to ascertain the child's wishes as to
11 his or her custodian and as to visitation. The court may permit counsel to be present
12 at the interview. The court shall cause a record of the interview to be made and to
13 be part of the record in the case.
14 (2) The court may seek the advice of professional personnel, whether or not employed
15 by the court on a regular basis. The advice given shall be in writing and made
16 available by the court to counsel upon request. Counsel may examine as a witness
17 any professional personnel consulted by the court.
18 (3) (a) Paid visitation supervisors and parenting coordinators in a custody
19 proceeding under this chapter, whether appointed by the court or engaged
20 by one (1) or more parties, shall document participation training focused on
21 the following:
22 1. Early childhood, child, and adolescent development;
23 2. Dynamics of domestic violence;

20 (1) If the court orders community-based outpatient mental health treatment under
21 this chapter, the court shall:

23 shall assemble a multidisciplinary team; and
24 (b) Report every order for community-based outpatient treatment issued under
25 this section to the Department for Behavioral Health, Developmental and
26 Intellectual Disabilities.
27 (2) (a) The multidisciplinary team shall:
Page 44 of 87
SB012220.100 - 1929 - XXXX 3/31/2026 4:08 PM Engrossed

UNOFFICIAL COPY 26 RS SB 122/EN
1 1. Regularly monitor the person's adherence to the conditions of the
2 order and regularly report this information to the court, the county
3 attorney, respondent's counsel, and any other party the court deems
4 necessary; and
5 2. Consist of three (3) mental health professionals, including any of the
6 following:
7 a. The respondent's doctor;
8 b. A nurse practitioner;
9 c. A prescriber;
10 d. A therapist;
11 e. A case manager;
12 f. A peer support specialist; or
13 g. Any other person deemed qualified by the court.
14 (b) Any responsible adult may report nonadherence to the conditions of the
15 order to the court, the county attorney, respondent's counsel, and any other
16 party the court deems necessary.
17 (3) Reports may be provided in written format, in person, or via electronic means, at
18 the court's discretion.
19 (4) The cabinet shall promulgate administrative regulations in accordance with KRS
20 Chapter 13A necessary to implement this section.

17 (1) (a) Upon motion of the county attorney under subsection (11)(a)2.b.ii. of

19 plan as soon as practicable to the court and the respondent's counsel of
20 record. The court, upon motion of the county attorney or the court's own
21 motion, shall conduct a review hearing:
22 1. To determine if the discharge plan gives the respondent a realistic
23 opportunity to avoid imminent readmittance into an inpatient
24 psychiatric hospital for treatment; and
25 2. At the earliest practicable time, consistent with due process and the
26 availability of counsel, and in no event later than seven (7) days after
27 the motion is made, except with the respondent's consent or upon the
Page 47 of 87
SB012220.100 - 1929 - XXXX 3/31/2026 4:08 PM Engrossed

UNOFFICIAL COPY 26 RS SB 122/EN
1 court's finding that extraordinary circumstances exist and that delay is
2 indispensable to protect the respondent and the community.
3 (b) This hearing shall only be conducted for a respondent who within the past
4 twelve (12) months has been found incompetent to stand trial in a criminal
5 proceeding and has not been committed under KRS Chapter 202C.
6 (2) The court shall verify that discharge planning procedures were completed to give
7 the respondent a realistic opportunity to avoid recurrence of substantial symptom
8 burden that would necessitate psychiatric hospitalization. Those procedures shall
9 include but not be limited to any of the following:
10 (a) Documenting the housing status of the respondent or that housing services
11 were offered and the respondent declined;
12 (b) Scheduling an outpatient treatment appointment for no later than seven (7)
13 days after discharge;
14 (c) Providing or prescribing a thirty (30) day supply of medication;
15 (d) Documenting a transportation plan that may include securing a bus pass,
16 taxi voucher, or an acknowledgment that the respondent will walk or the
17 respondent's family will provide transportation;
18 (e) Developing and documenting a crisis plan with contact information for
19 services that are available twenty-four (24) hours a day;
20 (f) Developing a transfer of care plan or attempting to develop a transfer of
21 care plan with the respondent if the respondent has met with an outpatient
22 provider or an appointment with the outpatient provider has been
23 scheduled; or
24 (g) Contacting the respondent's family or other support systems, if the
25 respondent consents.
26 (3) For respondents with decision-making capacity who refuse housing or other
27 services under subsection (2) of this section, the discharge plan shall document:
Page 48 of 87
SB012220.100 - 1929 - XXXX 3/31/2026 4:08 PM Engrossed

1 (a) That housing and other services were offered and explained;
2 (b) The respondent's reasons for refusal;
3 (c) That the respondent understands the potential consequences of his or her
4 choices;

6 contacts, mobile crisis services, drop-in services, and other safety-oriented
7 resources; and
8 (e) That there is a plan for periodic outreach to offer services.

6 (b) Current evaluations of the respondent's social, intellectual, physical, and
7 educational condition, adaptive behavior, and social skills. Such evaluations
8 may be based on prior evaluations not more than three (3) months old, except
9 that evaluations of the respondent's intellectual condition may be based on
10 individual intelligence test scores not more than one (1) year old;
11 (c) An opinion as to whether guardianship or conservatorship is needed, the type
12 of guardianship or conservatorship needed, if any, and the reasons therefor;
13 (d) An opinion as to the length of time guardianship or conservatorship will be
14 needed by the respondent, if at all, and the reasons therefor;
15 (e) If limited guardianship or conservatorship is recommended, a further
16 recommendation as to the scope of the guardianship or conservatorship,
17 specifying particularly the rights to be limited and the corresponding powers
18 and duties of the limited guardian or limited conservator;
19 (f) A description of the social, educational, medical, and rehabilitative services
20 currently being utilized by the respondent, if any;
21 (g) A determination whether alternatives to guardianship or conservatorship are
22 available;
23 (h) A recommendation as to the most appropriate treatment or rehabilitation plan
24 and living arrangement for the respondent and the reasons therefor;
25 (i) A listing of all medications the respondent is receiving, the dosage, and a
26 description of the impact of the medication upon the respondent's mental and
27 physical condition and behavior;

1 (j) An opinion whether attending a hearing on a petition filed under KRS

6 (5) The evaluation report may be compiled by a community center for mental health or

8 developmentally disabled persons, if the respondent is a resident of such facility, or

7 (a) Mental illness as defined by KRS 202A.011[(9)], or an intellectual disability

10 mental illness, intellectual disability, or disability renders the parent

12 psychological needs of the child for extended periods of time;

14 the family;
